However, most retail investors remained long. The future of the cotton market depends on gold prices and American cotton.

▲Hankou Mark Declines by More Than One Tael. In the opening session of the Hankou Mark market, due to the continuous decline in Indian cotton for two days, market sentiment was weak, and merchants closed out positions in large quantities, with declines ranging from 1.15 to 1.4 taels. In the afternoon, the market was slightly weak, with fluctuations ranging from up or down five fen to one qian. The total transaction volume for the day was 64,800 piculs. Yu Da sold 4,500 piculs, Chang Feng 7,900 piculs, Gong Ji 6,800 piculs, Shen Chang 3,700 piculs, Tong Xing 2,000 piculs, and Xie Sheng 2,100 piculs. Yu Da bought 5,600 piculs, Gong Tai 2,800 piculs, Shen Chang 2,400 piculs, Xin Cheng 6,900 piculs, and Yuan Da 2,200 piculs. The closing prices are recorded below:

The Reasons for Last Week's Firm Rise in American Cotton

▲Liverpool Market Situation Firm and Stable

▲Favorable Political Situation in India

▲Improvement in Raw Cloth Demand

A New York telegram on the 27th reported on the cotton market situation for the week: After a price correction before the holiday, the Liverpool market situation was firm and stable, and the Egyptian and Indian cotton markets also returned to their previous stability. The encouraging news from the Indian political situation and reports of activity in the domestic demand for American raw cotton cloth contributed to the rise in cotton prices. At the beginning of the week, Japanese purchases were a characteristic of the market, but when the October futures exceeded 12 cents, Japanese purchases stopped. A total of approximately 126,000 bales were delivered in March, all absorbed by large companies and cooperatives purchasing spot goods. Weather conditions east of Kansas were overcast and rainy, delaying field work, but cotton crop preparations were generally ahead of schedule, except in the far west and southern Texas. Although merchants were unwilling to buy as prices rose, believing that the shortage of fellow traders had greatly reduced and that prices might correct, the improving prospects for the textile trade made people reluctant to short.

▲Further News: The market situation is more stable for both sides than before, with slightly weaker buying and slightly reduced demand for spot cotton. Recently, there have been reports of considerable transactions in domestic piece goods trading, but prices have not matched the rise in cotton prices, and now there is a slight stagnation. High cotton prices, sufficient rainfall, and large government disbursements have led some to say that the reduction in cotton acreage may not be as large as expected. Arts

Recent Trends in French Literature - Man Ru

Jacques-Émile Blanche

Jacques-Émile Blanche is a well-known figure nationally and an important writer. He has published several novels, with his most recent, "Aymeris," considered his most significant work.

What kind of work is "Aymeris"?

Many say it is his autobiography, with the events mirroring his own life. For instance, the protagonist, Georges Aymeris, like Blanche himself, is a descendant of a noble Parisian family. Aymeris' father, a respected lawyer, resembles Blanche's father. While Blanche's father had a different profession than Aymeris' father in the book, he was a renowned psychiatrist. The reputations and status of the two are quite similar. Moreover, Blanche is a figure in the anecdotes of modern French literature, as he treated Maupassant's mental illness in his later years. Furthermore, like the protagonist, the author is also a painter and admired Manet (the famous Impressionist painter) twenty years before Manet gained recognition. Therefore, based on these points, some claim that this novel is Blanche's autobiography. However, these are just superficial reasons and cannot definitively prove that the work is indeed an autobiography. In reality, Jacques-Émile Blanche's "Aymeris," like many other writers' novels, draws from the author's memories for some of its elements. These elements have been modified and altered, differing from a straightforward autobiography. The novel depicts France between 1870 and 1914, offering an interesting panorama.

Among Young Writers

Two have already published their first and second works. Typically, after a new writer's debut work achieves fame, the second work often struggles to maintain that success. Therefore, the publication of the second work is a challenging and important milestone for young writers. If they can overcome this hurdle, their future position is greatly secured. The two writers we are discussing can both be considered as having successfully navigated this milestone. Their second works have achieved considerable success. Eugène Dabit's new work is "Little Louis." This novel, like his debut "Hotel du Nord," has a very simple plot. In August 1914, at the outbreak of the European War, Little Louis saw his father go off to war. His family was poor, and he had to work at home to support his mother. Several months passed, and these months were filled with anxiety, desires, and turmoil. Later, he also joined the army. His life was difficult and lonely. In a garrison town, he met a former colleague from the shop. This man's uncle ran a brothel, and Little Louis went there to work at night, washing dishes and glasses. The women there treated him as a companion. Later, he left the rear and was transferred to the front lines, where he experienced new hardships. After the armistice, he returned home, but old life started again from the beginning. The plot of the book is just like that. It is not easy to write ordinary events so lovely and touching. The second is Pierre Véry.

Pierre Véry

Véry's works are stylistically the opposite of Eugène Dabit's. His new book is poetic, somewhat wild, and both challenging and interesting, just like his debut work. This book is not suitable for those who enjoy clear and adventurous stories, but for those seeking unique poetic charm, Pierre Véry's new book is a delightful work.

Francis Carco, a writer from the Latin Quarter of Paris, is famous for his depictions of life there. He recently published a novel titled "The Street." The main character in this novel is still a French artist with a romantic temperament, but the subject matter is very novel. It can be described as a

Pirandello-esque Novel

We know that Pirandello is a modern Italian playwright famous for his novel subject matters and grotesque style. The subject matter of Francis Carco's new work is reminiscent of Pirandello's plays. The difference is that the stories written by Carco still have a realistic tone. Although novel, they are not necessarily without realism, so they do not give people a feeling of absurdity. The plot of the novel can be summarized as follows: A certain writer encounters a prostitute. Because he feels that this woman can be a wonderful subject for a novel, he develops a strong interest in her. He tries to make her fall in love with him, making her feel that he cares about her. Because she sees that he is more concerned about the kind of life of prostitution than some men, he obtains a lot of material from her and her life. But once all the material he wants to use in his planned novel has been gathered, his secret goal has been fully achieved, and he loses interest in her. Although he feels that he should not do this, he abandons her, violating her body and her soul. The ending is an inevitable tragedy. She dies miserably in a hospital.

André Malraux

André Malraux is one of the most outstanding new French writers. He can be said to belong to the "New Romantic" school. His works are a synthesis of wisdom, secularism, and resolute nihilism. The romantic sentiment is obvious. His new book, "La Voie Royale" (The Royal Way), is also a novel like that. This book is the first part of a series of novels that he intends to write. The future title of the series will be "The Forces of the Desert," "Les Puissances du Désert." As the name suggests, these are likely to be romantic novels with adventurous themes. "La Voie Royale" tells the story of a brave young Frenchman named Claude Vannec, who, due to financial ruin, cannot establish himself in his home country and goes to Siam. He has studied Eastern art and knows that in the unexplored jungles of Cambodia, there is an ancient road that has been forgotten. Along this road are many unknown temples. This road is "The Royal Way." In ancient times, it was the main thoroughfare for communication between the countries of Indochina. Vannec goes to Siam with the intention of exploring the jungle along this road. He hopes to discover some ancient Eastern bas-reliefs in those temples, which he can bring back to Europe in the future and sell as antiques to make a fortune. But this is an adventure with two layers of danger. First, since he will be going deep into the wilderness, he will inevitably clash with uncivilized natives. Second, if he wants to transport the discovered antiquities back to Europe, he will inevitably clash with the French authorities in Siam, because smuggling antiquities and works of art out of the country is strictly prohibited. But he is not afraid of either of these layers. He is determined to go on an adventure, originally because he wants to experience the taste of adventure and danger. The inevitability of struggle and resistance makes him feel eager to try even more. On the ship to Indochina, he meets a traveler. This man is older than him and has an even more worldly attitude. Claude Vannec proposes that they go together, promising to share the blessings and divide the spoils in the future. The man agrees. The novel ends here. What will happen next naturally has to wait for the second part.

This work should be classified under Romanticism because it has all the characteristics of romantic works. For example, passionate indulgence, rebellious emotions, the creation of one's own destiny, and the desire for destruction are all present. The characters in the book break away from modern society, embrace a fearless spirit, and go to create their own destiny, just like the works of the early Romantic era broke through the barriers of Classicism and expressed free and unrestrained emotions. Therefore, works like Vannec's can be said to be works of New Romanticism, only with a calm attitude, a dry tone, and a style similar to Naturalism. As for Vannec's beautiful language and rich poetic descriptions, they resemble the works of the Aesthetic Movement, exerting all the abilities of delicacy and beauty.
